7 
 SOCIAL ENGINEERING COUNTERMEASURES AND         
RISK MITIGATIONS 
 
 
In this chapter, we are going to talk about how we can defend against threats from the social engineer-
ing, in other words, we will talk about social engineering countermeasures we will look at different ap-
proaches. Risk mitigation in this context can be deﬁned as an action to reduce the probability of an ad-
verse event occurring as we have seen the result of our analysis in the last chapter or to reduce the ad-
verse consequences if it is happened, however, let us talk about our mitigation model in the next sec-
tion. 
 
7.1.1                  Mitigation Model 
 
The below figure 47 is our mitigation model. In order to mitigate the contributing factors in table 15, the 
organization should implement the factors listed under organization on the bellow figure 47. Employees 
also must comply with the items listed on the right side of the picture below, however for the rest of the 
chapter we will talk in detail about the two mitigation lists, listed on the below model figure 47. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
When we talk about countermeasures for social engineering we need to look at both electronic and so-
cially countermeasures to make clear what can we implement at the system level. As mention before in 
mitigation model, we divide the solution into two levels which are. 
Figure 53: Mitigation Model 
==PAGE:68==
Risk Analysis for Organizational Information in Relation Social  
Engineering attack   
 
1.  What organization should do to protect their systems?  
2. What employees should aware in terms of social engineer?  
 
How can we use technologies to defend against this risk but also how we address it socially, in addition 
how can we get the organizations/people who the target a social engineering to be more resilient to the 
threat? It is important to look at both options and as with many things in security, thus Let's start with 
the organizational side and talk about the employee SE awareness. 
 
 
7.1.2              Mitigation required by Organization's side 
 
7.1.2.1                      Employee SE awareness training 
 
Employees need security awareness training to learn who's a SE. A SE can be considered anyone as a per-
son, for example, someone you call by telephone and claim that he works the same organization but ac-
tually never worked in your organization (MITNICK, 2002). Employees should understand the potential 
consequences of pushing a link which he/she does not know and responding to a mail that need faster 
response. They should not respond if an employee is doubt and a mail is weird. Your organization need to 
create a security policy-program that engages, interacts, and dives deep into security awareness, for in-
stance showing how SE can quickly crack an easy password and showing impact of that security hole. The 
next picture cited from a report made by CONSULTIA (CONSULTIA, 2015). As we can see on the picture a 
largest percentage (56%) of the research answers are that most dangerous SE threat to organization is 
lack of employee awareness, therefore employee SE awareness training is important 
Factor for the mitigation of factors cause for SE attack. Let us move to talk the next mitigation factor 
namely, Security Policies  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
7.1.2.2                             Security Policies  
 
It is crucial important that the organization has a Security Policy (SP) (Pompon, 2016). When we are 
talking about security problems of SE, if the organization has a SP and let us say a SE attack has hap-
Figure 54: Percent of lack of employee awareness 
==PAGE:69==
Risk Analysis for Organizational Information in Relation Social  
Engineering attack   
 
pened, then the causal of security incident is definitely a violation of the SP, because the SP is a doc-
umented law-suites which is important for the employees to obey it. As an employee the SP will tell 
you or give you guidelines about what you are allowed to do and what is not allowed. One of the 
security policies can be “Do not click on an email link which you are unsure when you are using the 
organization's computers” or “It is not allowed to send a private email from the organization's net-
work”. Having SP will legalize or giving right for the organization to prosecute their employee who 
disobey SP rules, when a security exploitation occurs which is responsible an identified insider 
SE(employee), on the other hand if an organization has SP saying “The organization should provide 
at least one SE and security-awareness courses for their employees” and the organization did not 
do that, then they cannot prosecute employees for small mistakes, however an organization should 
have only one standard SP which may cover the hole organizations policy (Pompon, 2016). SP is also 
a standard procedure for the system of communication between the various administrative and 
employee sectors with regard to security, therefore having SP is important feature for risk imita-
tion. Next is separation of duties. 
 
7.1.2.3                              Separation of Duties 
 
Separation of duties is the concept of having more than one person required to complete a task 
(Kenin D. Mitnick & William L. Simon, 2005). To limit the privileges for accessing the resource or sys-
tem, it is important that employees have a different of duty and variety access privileges, then it 
will be easier to control, for example, a programmer make code changes and a system changes de-
ployment employee should be different people or persons as well as the normal login system moni-
toring and normal IT system (Pompon, 2016). The advantage of separation of duties include two 
things 
1. Traceability of occurrences, in case of system misuse 
2. Control of authorization 
 
It is also technique to segregate authorities for work operation and work records and requesting 
from the approval (Pompon, 2016). 
 
7.1.2.4                             Least Privilege 
 
The principle of least privilege requires that a process, a user, or a program must be able to access 
only the information and resources that are necessary for its legitimate purpose, otherwise if a sys-
tem user has administrator rights which is normally windows-based systems, then an insider SE may 
install a key logger or unintentionally accept malicious attachment which remotely monitoring the 
system activities and stealing passwords (Kenin D. Mitnick & William L. Simon, 2005), to mitigate SE 
causal factors you need to minimize privileges as much as possible. Another import factor is Access 
Control which is the next following section.  
 
==PAGE:70==
Risk Analysis for Organizational Information in Relation Social  
Engineering attack   
 
7.1.2.5                        Access control policy  
 
The organization should implement solid access control policy to protect the organization's assets/ 
information against unauthorized access (Pompon, 2016). These unauthorized actors may include 
organization's employee which can be insider social engineer. The most important focus areas in 
controlling system access are: 
1.  Security Configuration and  
2.  User Access Administration.  
 
Although for SE, can steal access passwords using techniques we talked chapter 4, however, it is im-
portant that at the application level, the system security configuration should effectively control the 
desired types of access, namely read, write and update, in addition administration procedures must 
restricted these access types to currently authorized users. We are also talking about digital access 
control which controls how many times may user can test his login password in case he/she has for-
gotten? how long time this password can be valid? what are the specific criteria when creating a 
password? In our case, since the organization use online system connected to the database, then 
the database used by the application must be configured an access policy to restrict only access to 
authorized administrative. 
 
7.1.2.6                          Role based access control (RBAC) 
 
RBAC is security mechanism which the only authorized user has the access to the information, in 
addition RBAC maintains access authentication and authorization at the same time, thus RBAC is 
most commonly used as access control. Since it is based on user role privilege it supports non-repu-
diation security element, otherwise there may be a possible denial of performed actions, however, 
in case for SE used shoulder surfing scenario to steal user's password, then this RBAC cannot stop 
the crime, however it may localize the office and the computer within the organization. 
An access control can also be different methods such physical life access control or the system re-
quires you to swipe a key card, scan device, face recognition or finger print.  A physical access con-
trol is also an important access control, because it can stop as Tailgating SE technique. Next section 
is about strong password. 
 
7.1.2.7                                  Strong Password  
 
It is important that a user's password not to be easily guessable, and it should be used both in the 
alphabet and numbers. It should be strong password. Many cyber attackers try to guess any online 
system that requires a password, so if your password is simple that means it is vulnerable for any 
intruder both insider and online ones. 
 
 
==PAGE:71==
Risk Analysis for Organizational Information in Relation Social  
Engineering attack   
 
7.1.2.8                                 Record Destruction 
 
Social engineers delighted to get their hands-on records of anything that gives them any connection 
with their target for example, personally identifiable thing like the information about people work 
in an organization or organizational strategies or even internal find directories for companies all of 
these things are enormously valuable to the social engineers, therefore proper record destruction is 
absolutely essential.  
We divided record destructions into three categories namely, paper records, digital records, and 
electronic records which we will talk shortly in the following sections.  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
As mentioned the figure 49 depicts the categorize data records for three types which are a paper 
records, digital records, and electronic devices. Firs let us talk about a paper record. 
 
7.1.2.8.1 
                                   Paper record 
 
A paper record is what gets literally and physically put in the trash-can on the someone's desk. A 
paper records that are no longer required need to be destroyed properly, it has to be shredded, 
that means what is inside should be shredded, that may include things like bank information credit 
card data or any sensitive data which organization does not want anyone else getting their hands 
on. Don’t just throw that in your normal trash can, then maybe someone else possibly later, having 
the ability to read these documents. Things like plastics, CDs, credit cards, you need to use a de-
signed shredder-machine such cross cut shredder.  
 
7.1.2.8.2 
                               Digital Record 
 
We need to properly get rid of data to the no longer required also we have to securely erases digital 
records, however normal deleting files operating system often does not permanently erase digital 
data, therefore, to erase data permanently organizations have to use specialized software such 
Figure 55: Record Destruction 
==PAGE:72==
Risk Analysis for Organizational Information in Relation Social  
Engineering attack   
 
DBAN, HD shredder or Headers which are going through a process for re-moving magnetic fields 
from disk. If organization destroy their data in that manner then they may mitigate risk of SE. 
 
7.1.2.8.3 
                              Electronic devices 
 
Organizations need to destroy electronic devices which are no longer required to work again. Physi-
cal devices such hard-disk, printers and photocopies should be dismantled effectively as being an 
inoperable state, however you should never just have thrown in the trash, then someone (figure 
23) picks it applied around and extracts digital records, therefore organizations must regularly de-
stroy items that contain electronic records by using such industrial machines with a sledgehammer 
that smashing devices to small pieces that would be impossible for intruder to piece together again. 
Doing that way, you may mitigate risk of SE attack. 
7.1.2.9                                  Regular updates 
 
It is important for any organization to update their systems periodically, because the attackers and 
SEs are always trying hard to use structured ways to crack their targets, moreover a new security 
patches use to update the old existing ones and these new updated version is compatible with the 
new operating systems which has upgraded security issues, therefore whenever the organization 
uses an old version of security patches they are risking for malicious attack and viruses also their 
security is vulnerable (Christopher Hadnagy, 2011). Operating system and software companies are 
always trying to protect and secure their systems if you do not renew and update the organization's 
systems that may result in security holes for your organization, therefore regular updating is one of 
SE countermeasures.  
 
7.1.2.10 
                             Monitoring and Review 
 
A SE risk cannot be eliminated to 0 with regard to its contemporary phenomenal, but when the or-
ganization establishes the control we talked so far, it is very important to monitor and review the 
outcome of that control (Pompon, 2016). How the control is function according to its specifications, 
its efficiency, and whether it is effective, in other words, if the control reduced the risk the organi-
zation experienced before, the monitoring and reviewing are good options to mitigate factors for SE 
attack. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:73==
Risk Analysis for Organizational Information in Relation Social  
Engineering attack   
 
7.1.3                   Mitigation required by Employee side 
 
7.1.3.1               spear phishing and Business email compromise (bec) 
 
In the subsequent sections we will talk about how to avoid these targeted spearfishing campaigns 
that we demonstrated in chapter four when they come to your employees in your organization or 
to one of your family members. These activities are not something that can be done by the organi-
zation, instead it is an activity that must be avoided as each person in the organization, so it is con-
cern individuals not organization. Organizations cannot control by individual’s behaviors. 
 
7.1.3.2                        Hover over the address 
 
 The organizations’ employees should to hover over the addresses of any suspicious email and look 
before they ever click through. Never click through a suspicious e-mail especially when it has some-
thing looks like a Facebook icon at some weird number as we talked in chapter four.  
Instead of clicking through any email any time especially if it has an urgent message if this is said 
“Hi, Farah you're in some inappropriate pictures on Facebook “or can't believe someone said this 
about you or it looks like your account has been hacked. You need to log in to verify that it's you. 
What you need to do is get in your browser and type in www.Facebook dot com.  
 
7.1.3.3                  Check for secure communication (https) 
 
Besides typing in the full address, the second thing that we need to do is check to make sure that it 
is secure that you are using https:// whenever we enter our username and password.  There is a 
small difference in the URL but it is an enormous difference in the security of the website. Like this 
https Facebook, domainnames:// or the name of your bank that secure connection means that it is 
encrypted and no one can just pull your username and password from it. We can also notice that 
it's going to the real website address not to attend at 192.9.0.21 or 127.0.0.1 dot something us we 
have seen on the phishing mail I experimented in chapter four or another web server halfway 
around the world that's trying to steal your credentials. Checking that you may mitigate risk of SE 
attack. 
 
7.1.3.4                    Bookmark frequently used websites 
 
It is always safer if you just bookmark those web sites you visit frequently. So, if you click my book-
mark on your browser and say you want to bookmark Gmail, Facebook, Dansk Bank, Nordea or 
whatever your bank, maybe if you've bookmarked them, then, the benefit of doing that is that all 
you have to do is come to my bookmarks and open up that Dansk Bank account or come to my 
bookmarks and open up Facebook from the secure logon page.  
==PAGE:74==
Risk Analysis for Organizational Information in Relation Social  
Engineering attack   
 
If you book market then you just come to your most important pages like Yahoo, Facebook or 
Google or you chat or whatever it may be Amazon, whatever your bank account information is. 
When you bookmark those, it will also help you to avoid typing errors, however if that organization 
has a few extra misspellings of its name then that might take you to a malicious website. The typos 
are pretty common when it comes to typing in web sites so type it correctly. Confirm that you have 
got a secure web site and then book market so that you do not ever have to wonder if you are go-
ing to the right site. 
 
7.1.3.5                          NEVER CLICK LINK 
 
When it comes to the link from an email never click through even if you hover over it. Maybe it 
looks good like our other ones. It looked good www.facebook.com as something do not click 
through the link come to your browser and either type it in and make sure it's secure. Or it is better 
yet to bookmarked as we talked in last section, so that you can come back to as safely in the future. 
As organizations security trainer you especially want to educate your organization co-workers that 
if something in the email seems urgent like “hey you need to log in now to get this or if something's 
giving something away for free” then you need to make sure to tell them never to click through the 
link. They have to go to Facebook.com and search from there.  
One more time, never click through a suspicious e-mail and be suspicious of every e-mail even 
when it looks like it's coming from a friend. For example, if your friend sends you something that 
says hey looks like you've been hacked or somebody posted an inappropriate picture of you or did 
you really say this comment on this social media platform because your friend's account may have 
been hacked. Remember that it can come from that other person's account or it can be spoofed to 
look like it is coming from your friends account as you have seen in the spear-phishing case study in 
chapter 5.  
As a reader of this thesis, you have to be really careful whenever you receive anything by e-mail if it 
is coming from a friend. Instead, why don't you just text them or call them. You have to confirm 
that they don't need help in real life but spear phishers scamers.con artists predators are getting 
smarter and smarter all the time. We saw just a handful of ways to make an email look like it was 
really coming from a social media web site and not from our fake spearfishing server that we set up 
in Kali Linux in chapter four. So as organizational security personal you really need to be careful 
when it comes to phishing. 
Again as security officer/trainer, train employees to remember that they can just click on a new 
browser window and type in the address directly. Make sure that it is secure when you get there 
and you can verify that with a little lock, see the next figure 50 from my bank address.

7.1.3.6                        Never plug in unknown USB 
 
Do not just pick up a founded USB drive or accept a free download or free software. Sometimes 
that click can take you or your organization to a website that is compromised. Specifically, if you 
plug in unknown USB you may allow SE Baiting technique and malicious software spread in hole sys-
tem.  
 
 
7.1.3.7                         Use Different passwords 
 
Another very important point is the CEO and employees to use different passwords in their work 
and their private access-required systems also use different passwords if you have different ac-
counts, because if a hacker breaks an access to one of your accounts the others can be also ac-
cessed as well. 
 
7.1.3.8                           Change passwords 
 
One good tactic is to change your password when you use it for a while or frequently, because a SE 
or hacker may get knowledge of your password and he is lurking to get a good opportunity to do 
some bad things or theft in your account but if you change frequently so SE and hackers are having 
trouble for learning your password. 
 
7.1.3.9                           Never share password 
 
Your password should be something that knows only you, so never share with any other person. If 
you share your password, then if something bad used for your password that will be up to you, be-
cause the point is the password is only private for you and should not be shared with another per-
son. 
The systems at the software layer not necessarily always to stop social engineering from happening 
at all, but sometimes to minimize the risk of it or to better enables to respond when social engi-
neering attack does occur,  
 
7.1.3.10 
     Install NetCraft, Stop Phishing and Phishing Detector 
 
To have an extra protection in yourself and the organization you working, you can download an 
extension like the Netcraft, Stop Phishing and Phishing Detector toolbars for Firefox for Chrome for 
whatever your favorite browser may be and it can help you spot those bad you are elves that you 
might try to click through in your organization.

7.1.3.10.1      NETCRAFT  
 
 
 
  
 
As we talked before in chapter four, the Netcraft toolbar will allow you to install an extension in 
your Firefox or chrome or another browser window. Netcraft will help you spot fake phishing emails 
a little more quickly. So, if you get something from a server that people know is a bad server then 
Netcraft can give you a little advisory. When you hit suspected website, Netcraft will notice you say-
ing this phishing site has been blocked by the Netcraft toolbar.  
Once again phishing has gotten much and much more difficult to spot, therefore be careful with 
every email be selfish suspicious of any email even if it looks like it is from your bank from your or-
ganization from your email provider or your social media platform or even from one of your friends 
or family members because they could have been hacked themselves. Sometimes these tools can 
go a long way toward preventing the types of social engineering attacks that we have been dis-
cussed in this thesis.  
 
 
 
7.1.3.10.2 Stop Phishing    
 
 
 
                                  
 
To get a phishing warning, it is important to install Stop Phishing extension in your browser. If you 
do so, the extension Stop phishing and will tell you if you open fraudulent email or website, it will 
even make a report to all phishing mails and website you visited. 
 
7.1.3.10.3 Phishing Detector    
       
                                     
 
 
 
 
Phishing detector is another powerful extension for all browsers. It has been designed to warn the 
user about online banking phishing scams. It is really useful browser extension. When I did test on 
my bank it got the picture you see an appendix D, so it is very important that you install this exten-
sion. 
 
7.1.3.11 
           Preventing BEC Scams 
 
➢ Firstly, do not take fast decisions to wire money. 
➢ Secondly, before you make any transfer you need to know who are you contacting, do your 
best verification you can may be including to call the CEO. 
➢ Organization should implement Intrusion Detection System, because Intrusion Detection 
System has the power to filter mails and flag some emails, like those looks like the organiza-
tion’s mails, however not the real organizations mail.

7.2                        Conclusion  
 
In this chapter we have talked a lot about protecting your organization even yourself, your family, 
and friends from social engineering. We started with mitigation model which includes two sides 
mitigation recommendations, namely employees and organizations. The organization side mitiga-
tion include(Employee SE awareness Training, Create Security Policies, Separation of Duties, Least 
Privilege, Access Control Policy, Record Destruction, Regular Updates, and Monitoring and Review) 
The employee side mitigation include (Hover over the address before clicking, Never Click Link, 
Check for secure Communication (HTTPS), bookmark always, Never plug in Unknown USB, Use Dif-
ferent Passwords, Change Passwords, Never Share Password, Installing three web extensions and 
finally preventing BEC Scams ) 
 Attacks like spearfishing some really scary things out on the Internet specially organization’s online 
information. However, you can be safer by always being suspicious of emails never clicking through 
any links and e-mails especially if there is a sense of urgency or sense that you are getting some-
thing for free or something exclusive always go out to the web browser and typing your favorite e-
commerce site. Type in your bank account or your bank website. Type in your email account. Never 
click through those links especially with a suspicious you are. And if you want an extra layer of pro-
tection. Use a tool like Netcraft toolbar.

8.2                              DISCUSSION  
 
In connection with our theoretical framework which is associated with this research literature. We 
can say that the results reflect the current technologies and literature we reviewed so far because 
as normally, people use OSINT in their daily routine and do not much concerned, such SE attacks, 
consequently, we got the results to the answers of questions throughout this Thesis research which 
scaring the danger of the possible SE attack. 
I believe the mitigation model presented in Chapter 7 offers a lot of benefits for organizations and 
employees as well because it clearly shows a reader the mitigation duties recommended from the 
organization and also mitigation duties recommended for employees separately, thus applying 
model 7.1.1, the employees and organization know what they have to be careful in relation to SE 
The results from the case study in chapter 5. are undoubtedly correct, because we obtained them 
through a real interview with a real organization, therefore the result is not an estimate and just 
theoretically. 
Finally, I believe that our findings have a great advantage in this field of our research concerned as 
well as professionals, because the Thesis includes practical experiments and presented their results, 
explain what happened and the tools and technologies may SE are used. 
 
 
 
8.3                              CONCLUSION  
 
The world is quickly switching from analog to digital which has significantly integrated everything, 
including workplaces, home devices, all kinds of medical equipment, especially in developed 
countries this technological change is presently integrated the whole life, however, this transitional 
change has challenges which are growing global cyber-security attackers and Social Engineering 
scams. 
As stated in the research purpose, the task of this thesis was to analyze publicly available 
organization's footprint, in addition, to answer questions listed in the purpose section 1.1, which 
==PAGE:81==
Risk Analysis for Organizational Information in Relation Social  
Engineering attack   
 
are also as a form of goals in section 1.3. In the report, we answered all the questions and we also 
achieved all the goals, in addition, we propose a very useful mitigation model, which concerns both 
employees and organizations. 
• 
In chapters 2 + 4, we achieved the goal of "Learn how easy it is to determine the hierarchy 
and internal structures and procedures in an organization" in chapter two we explained 
how it is possible for SE to discover the hierarchy and internal structure of the organization 
using the organizational chart, organizations' online information structure and their 
communication manner, also in chapter four, we have demonstrated how an SE practically 
can use social media to discover this information 
• 
In chapter 3, we achieve the goal of “Identify existing intelligence tools for open source 
intelligence gathering and social engineering”. We very deeply talked about the most 
important OSINT that frequently used today, in addition, we explain how a cyber attacker or 
SE can use those OSINTs to exploit organizational systems and individuals as well. 
• 
In chapter 4 we achieved the goal of "Identifying people of importance in the 
organization". We explained in detail, how a cyber-attacker that uses an OSINT can get the 
key persons who work in the organization either to be a low-level employee or top people 
such CEO, moreover, in chapter five we demonstrated different practical examples and 
techniques of spear-phishing attacks. 
 
• 
In chapter six, we achieved the goal of "Identity organizations risk from social engineering" 
we conduct an empirical research case study to analyze risks, and finally, based upon the 
result of the case study analysis, we identified the risks of SE. 
• 
In chapter seven, we talked about how we can mitigate risks from SE, we proposed our 
mitigation model. our model has two sides duties which are recommended to implement 
both the employee and organizations aspects of the SE implement 
After the completion of this thesis, I am very satisfied with the results we achieved, and I believe 
that the mission has successfully completed as mush possible, in other words, due to the time 
limitation, we could not talk or experiment with everything related to SE, however, the thesis 
successfully completed to all the purpose objects. I believe and I also hope, this thesis to be 
beneficial to both organizations and individuals as well.

Appendix  
 
 
B 
 
RISK 
1. Does your organization concerns about a risk of social engineering event occurrence? 
2. Does the organization concern about risks of insider social engineer attack? 
3. Does the organization offer an employee training to avoid risk of unawareness of social 
engineering? 
4. Does the organization concern about risks of malware infection on the organization's 
computers? 
5. To reduce risks, does the organization use electronic security systems, including antivirus 
software, firewall, intrusion detection, surveillance camera, etc.? 
6. Does the organization concern about risks of denial of service? 
7. Does the organization concerns about the risk of data theft caused by social engineering 
that may damage the confidentiality, integrity and availability of the organization's 
assets? 
8. does the organization have a strong data access control policy to strength data access 
authentication, authorization and to avoid risk of social engineering? 
9. Has the organization purchased or considered purchasing cyber liability insurance to 
avoid risk of paying huge compensation in case of damage

social engineering?

computers?

antivirus software, firewall, intrusion detection, surveillance camera, etc.?

APPENDIX 
 F 
 
 
 
The Social-Engineer Toolkit (SET) Report Generator 
 
Report generated by the Social-Engineer Toolkit 
Welcome to the Social-Engineer Toolkit Report Generation Tool. This report should contain 
information obtained during a successful phishing attack and provide you with the website and all of 
the parameters that were harvested. Please remember that SET is open-source, free, and available to 
the information security community. Use this tool for good, not evil. 
Social Engineering is defined as the process of deceiving people into giving away access or 
confidential information.  
 
Wikipedia defines it as: "is the act of manipulating people into performing actions or divulging 
confidential information. While similar to a confidence trick or simple fraud, the term typically 
applies to trickery or deception for the purpose of information gathering, fraud, or computer system 
access; in most cases the attacker never comes face-to-face with the victim."  
 
We consider social engineering to be the greatest risk to security. 
Report Statistics 
The credential harvester keeps track of how many individuals visited a site and those who actually 
fell for the attack. A total number of 20 individuals visited the site. Based on the total number of 20 
visitors, there was a total number of 77 victims that successfully fell for the attack.  
Report Findings Below:
